## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law describes how concentration changes over time, typically following power-law, exponential, or more complex mechanistic rate expressions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Reaction rate independent of concentration'}
- {'name': 'First-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)'}
- {'name': 'Second-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to square of concentration (bimolecular reaction)'}
- {'name': 'nth-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'General power-law rate expression for fractional or integer order reactions'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order with offset', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Competing first and second order pathways'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order forward and zero-order reverse (or approach to equilibrium)'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Logistic-type autocatalysis where product catalyzes the reaction'}
- {'name': 'Substrate inhibition kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2)', 'scenario': 'Enzyme kinetics with substrate inhibition at high concentrations'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent deactivation rate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Reaction with catalyst deactivation or time-varying rate constant'}
- {'name': 'Power-law with equilibrium shift', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * (A**c1 - c2)', 'scenario': 'Reaction approaching a non-zero equilibrium concentration'}
- {'name': 'Parallel reactions with different orders', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2', 'scenario': 'Multiple simultaneous reaction pathways consuming the same reactant'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive reaction intermediate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t)', 'scenario': 'Intermediate species in a consecutive reaction scheme A→B→C'}
- {'name': 'Rational rate law (Langmuir-Hinshelwood type)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)**2', 'scenario': 'Surface-catalyzed reaction with competitive adsorption'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate of concentration change (consumption) → dA_dt typically has a negative leading coefficient when A is a reactant being consumed
- Concentration power law order → The exponent on A in dA_dt = c*A^n reflects the molecularity or effective reaction order
- Equilibrium approach → Terms like (A - A_eq) or (A^n - c) indicate the system approaches a steady-state or equilibrium concentration
- Denominator with concentration terms → Rational expressions in A suggest surface catalysis, enzyme mechanisms, or adsorption-limited kinetics
- Time explicitly in rate expression → Explicit t-dependence (e.g., exp(c*t)) suggests non-autonomous systems like catalyst deactivation or external forcing
- Product of concentration and complement → A*(c-A) structure indicates autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics with a carrying capacity
- Sum of exponential decays in time → Multiple exponential terms in t suggest parallel or consecutive reaction pathways with distinct rate constants
- Square root or fractional power of concentration → A**0.5 or A**c with c<1 suggests dissociative mechanisms or diffusion-limited kinetics

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.5475*A² - 0.5475*A*exp(-0.0371*t) + 0.7049*cos(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three terms:
1. A quadratic term in A: `-0.5475*A²`
2. An exponential decay term: `-0.5475*A*exp(-0.0371*t)`
3. A cosine of logarithm term: `0.7049*cos(log(A+1))`

This is a very specific combination of basis functions. Let me check each candidate for the presence of these three types of terms.

Key observations:
- The `cos(log(A+1))` term is highly distinctive and cannot be replicated by polynomials, exponentials, or simple trigonometric functions.
- Any candidate that lacks a `cos(log(...))` or equivalent term cannot match.

Let me quickly scan for candidates that have `cos(log(...))` or `sin(log(...))` terms (since `cos(x) = sin(x + π/2)`):

- **Candidate 5**: has `sin(c6*log(c7*t + 1) + c8)` — this is `sin(log(t+...))`, not `sin(log(A+...))`. **NO MATCH** (wrong variable inside log).
- **Candidate 9**: has `sin(c3*log(c4*t + 1) + c5)` — again log of t, not A. **NO MATCH**.
- **Candidate 88**: has `sin(c3*log(A*c4 + 1))` — this is `sin(log(A+...))`. Let me check more carefully.
- **Candidate 109**: has `log(A*c4 + 1)` but multiplied by `A^c0*c1`. Not cos/sin of log.
- **Candidate 127**: has `sin(c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6)` — this is promising!

Let me analyze the promising candidates in detail:

### Candidate 88:
`A²*c0 + A*c1 + c2*sin(c3*log(A*c4 + 1)) + c5*exp(c6*t)`

GT = `-0.5475*A² - 0.5475*A*exp(-0.0371*t) + 0.7049*cos(log(A+1))`

This has:
- `A²*c0` ✓ (matches `-0.5475*A²`)
- `A*c1` — this is a constant times A, but GT has `A*exp(-0.0371*t)`, not just `A`. **NO MATCH** — can't represent `A*exp(αt)` with just `A*c1`.
- `c2*sin(c3*log(A*c4+1))` — with c3=1, c4=1, this gives `sin(log(A+1))`. But GT has `cos(log(A+1))`. Using phase: `sin(log(A+1) + π/2) = cos(log(A+1))`, but there's no phase shift constant here. Actually wait, `sin(c3*log(A*c4+1))` — if c3=1, this is just `sin(log(A+1))`, no phase shift available. **NO MATCH**.

Actually, I need to reconsider. `cos(x) = sin(x + π/2)`, but the candidate has `sin(c3*log(...))` with no additive phase constant. So it can't produce `cos(log(...))` unless we allow c3 to be complex, which we don't. **NO MATCH**.

Wait — actually `sin(c3*log(A*c4+1))` with c3 and c4 free... if c3 ≠ 1, this changes the frequency inside the sin, not the phase. So no, this can't match cos(log(A+1)). **NO MATCH**.

### Candidate 127:
`(c0 + c1*(c2*exp(c3*t) + 1)*sin(c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6))/(c2*exp(c3*t) + 1)`

Simplify: `c0/(c2*exp(c3*t) + 1) + c1*sin(c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6)`

This gives:
- `c1*sin(c4*log(A*c5+1) + c6)` — with c4=1, c5=1, c6=π/2: `c1*cos(log(A+1))` ✓
- `c0/(c2*exp(c3*t) + 1)` — this is a logistic-type function of t only.

But GT needs: `-0.5475*A² - 0.5475*A*exp(-0.0371*t)` in addition to the cos term.

The candidate has NO A² term and no A*exp(t) term. **NO MATCH**.

Now let me systematically go through all remaining candidates. Given the distinctive `cos(log(A+1))` term, I need candidates that can produce all three basis functions: A², A*exp(αt), and cos(log(A+1)).

None of the other candidates contain `cos(log(...))` or `sin(log(...))` with A as the argument (with a phase shift available).

Let me verify there's no hidden way to produce `cos(log(A+1))` from other functions. This function is transcendental and cannot be produced by:
- Polynomials in A
- exp(A) or exp(A²)
- sin(A) or cos(A)
- log(A+1) alone
- A^c (power functions)
- Rational functions of A

So any candidate without an explicit `sin/cos(log(A+...))` structure cannot match.

Let me check all candidates with sin/cos of log:
- Candidate 5: sin(log(t+...)) — wrong variable
- Candidate 9: sin(log(t+...)) — wrong variable  
- Candidate 22: sin(log(t+...)) — wrong variable
- Candidate 88: sin(log(A+...)) but no phase shift and missing A*exp(t)
- Candidate 127: sin(log(A+...)+c6) ✓ for cos term, but missing A² and A*exp(t)

None can match all three required terms simultaneously.
